Overseas Chinese Federation Held a Public Banquet Last Night

Preparing to Build a Memorial Stele for Chen Minqing 120

The Overseas Chinese Federation held a reception at the East Asia Restaurant last night because Chen Minqing, chairman of the Nanyang Penang Guanghua Daily, Reading Newspaper Agency, Zhenling Zhonghua, and Singapore Xin Guomin Daily, returned to China to discuss overseas Chinese affairs in Nanyang and prepare to build a memorial stele for martyr Chen Xinzheng. The Overseas Chinese Federation was established in the first year of the Republic of China by revolutionary overseas Chinese Chen Xinzheng, Wu Shirong, and others in accordance with the intentions of the Premier. This time, Chen Xinzheng's younger brother, Chen Minqing, negotiated in Beijing, and the central government commemorated Chen Xinzheng's revolutionary achievements and instructed the Fujian Provincial Party Department to cooperate with the government to build a Chen Xinzheng memorial stele in Xiamen Zhongshan Park. Chen Minqing, as a family member, is going to Xiamen today to assist. The Overseas Chinese Federation specially invited people from all walks of life to the banquet. Chairman Xu Jigong and Lin Youren first gave welcome speeches, followed by speeches from the guests. Finally, the Overseas Chinese Federation distributed the biography of Chen Xinzheng as follows:

Martyr Chen, named Wentu, zi (style name) Xinzheng, was a native of Siming Heshan in Fujian. He loved learning and had great aspirations and was valued by many in his hometown. At the age of nineteen, he followed his father Chen Yuhe to Nanyang to Penang to assist in the shipping business and also ran a business called Baocheng. In a few years, he started his business by transporting local products. The martyr did not confine himself to business. At that time, the Qing government was weak and the national situation was precarious. The Premier advocated revolution overseas and came to Nanyang from Tokyo. The martyr heard of it and jumped up and first welcomed him with overseas Chinese comrades Huang Quanguang, Wu Shirong, Qiu Mingyong, etc. Then there was the establishment of the Tongmenghui (Revolutionary Alliance). The martyr was young, shrewd, capable, and thoughtful in planning things. He was elected as a leader in the alliance. At the time of the initial defeat in Huizhou Qinlian, the leaders were all angry and advocated rapid advancement. The martyr gathered comrades and first raised thousands of gold to support the Premier and Keqiang to return to China. Then there was the Battle of Zhennanguan. Although the matter did not succeed, the morale was further stimulated. The martyr especially took action to organize the Penang Reading Newspaper Agency with comrades, as an opportunity to call on heroes and communicate public opinion, and actively prepared to support the party members in the country. Then there was the Northern Expedition of Hekou. Later, the Hekou Party army collapsed without support, and 500 heroes were disarmed by the French government and passed through Annam, wandering to Nanyang, shabby and almost inhuman. The martyr feared that the Han Chinese warriors would lose their dignity, and immediately raised thousands of yuan to purchase clothing, so that they could change their clothes and guide them on the shore. Chinese and foreign residents saw that their clothing was uniform and their steps were neat, and they all respected them. The impression of revolutionary soldiers was deeply rooted in the minds of overseas Chinese. Later, party members from the mainland came to Nanyang in increasing numbers to promote fundraising and worked hard. The martyr and others were responsible for providing for their travel. The martyr also saw the indispensability of a public opinion organ, so he organized the Guanghua Daily with his comrades. Mr. Hu Hanmin happened to be on the island and asked him to write the stock prospectus and rules and regulations, which took several months to succeed. When Guanghua Daily was published, the martyr was elected as the general manager, and Lei Tieya and Zhang Dujuan presided over the editorial office. Later, Lei Tieya wrote a letter introducing comrades Song Dunchu and Dai Tianchou to take editorial responsibility. When Dai Tianchou came, Shouyin (referring to Tang Shouqian) occupied Wuhan and the uprising was stopped. Our party in Penang was able to establish a clear banner and wage a war of hearts with the opposition party, starting from this time. One year before the Republic of China, the Guangzhou Uprising was newly defeated and Ni Yingdian died. The Premier returned to Penang from Yokohama and reorganized the Tongmenghui on a larger scale as the headquarters of the Nanyang provinces. The martyr assisted day and night, never tired, and his examination of things was often to the point, and the comrades all believed in him, and the Premier especially regarded him as an assistant. At that time, the Premier lived in Penang, and comrades from overseas and inland came to discuss matters, and they saw each other on the road. All the hospitality, travel expenses, and travel expenses were subsidized by the martyr and his comrades. The Premier and his family lived at No. 404, Sikan Street Garden Side, and the monthly rent and daily expenses were also borne by the martyr and others. Then the Premier was expelled by the Siamese and British governments, and was rejected by the government of the dependent territories.

Page 14

He went to the Americas, and his family still lived in Penang, and all the expenses were still borne by the martyr and others. When Guangzhou failed, the elite were lost, and the comrades were all depressed and unable to recover. The Premier was worried and gathered Keqiang, Hanmin, Boxian, etc. in Penang to plan things, and was worried about economic difficulties. One day at the meeting, the martyr gave a generous speech at the table, urging the comrades with righteousness, and everyone was grateful. On the same day, he raised 8,000 gold and went to the provinces to raise funds, and he got 50,000 to 60,000 yuan in a few days, and the distant roads came every day. The Premier was able to get a comprehensive plan and set up an agency in Hong Kong to plan a major event. Before long, there was the Huanghuagang Uprising, which shocked the whole country. It was said that the Huanghuagang Uprising was the driving force behind the Wuchang Uprising, and the Penang comrades were the mainstay of the Huanghuagang Uprising, and the martyr was the mainstay. Months after the failure of the Huanghuagang Uprising, the news of the concentration of party members in Wuhan reached Nanyang. The martyr urgently summoned his comrades to actively raise funds, day and night, and sent tens of thousands of yuan to the Hong Kong headquarters before and after. The two provinces of Min and Yue subsidized each other's relief, and at the same time reorganized the Tongmenghui and organized the Overseas Chinese Bomb Team, the Northern Expedition Team, and the Gendarmerie Team. Driven by righteous indignation, people competed to die, and those who volunteered to return to the country to join the army followed in the way, all of which was the strength of the martyr's advocacy. After the restoration of Fujian, the martyr was elected by the comrades in each port as the representative to return to Fujian and arrived in Fuzhou and saw that everything was waiting to be done and urgently needed money. He immediately sent a telegram to Nanyang to ask for money. Each port received the martyr's telegram and raised money by telegram. Rangoon, Singapore, Penang, Java, and the Philippines all sent tens of thousands of yuan. The Fujian governor was greatly surprised and asked the martyr to represent the province to raise Nanyang public bonds, and the amount of money was quite large. He was so brave and trustworthy in the face of things. After the North and South were unified, the Tongmenghui reorganized the Kuomintang headquarters and sent Lu Zhiyi to Nanyang to reorganize party affairs. The martyr and Zhiyi ran to the British and Dutch colonies, calling on comrades and spreading the party's principles. Although the party affairs could not be made public due to the obstruction of the governments of the provinces, the wind spread and the people's hearts were shaken. Before long, Yuan Shikai became emperor and the Song case occurred. The martyr advocated the crusade against Yuan and advocated fundraising. Comrades at home and abroad responded in droves. However, justice was subject to power, and the crusade against Yuan failed. Martyr Chen Xinzheng

He is a party member with weak will, either changing his mind or disheartened. The martyr jumped up and said, "If you don't meet the deep-rooted trees, you can't see the sharp weapon. Although politics is impossible, education and industry are the foundation of governance. The affairs of the world are very important, and there are many ways to serve the country. Don't be discouraged, Tongnan." Because he actively advocated education, he donated all the profits from his private business to schools, and for the comrades who were exiled to the south at home and abroad, he tried to mediate the teaching positions in various schools to spread revolutionary seeds, and planned with Qiu Mingchang and others to organize the Xin Guomin Daily in Singapore, and greatly Zhang Qihui made a fierce attack on the Northern Warlords. Its scale was large, and its handling was firm and decisive. After the defeat of the Second Revolution, the Premier organized the Chinese Revolutionary Party in Tokyo and appointed the martyr as the Penang branch chief. The soldiers in Nanyang were sent to the new party organization without expressing sympathy. There were almost Tokyo faction and Nanyang faction in the party. The martyr reconciled in the middle and explained the misunderstanding, but it took hard work. At that time, Fujian was ruled by Li Houji, gathering and killing people and living a miserable life. The Minnan comrades secretly carried out the movement to overthrow Li and crusade against Yuan, but some advocated not cooperating with the Chinese Revolutionary Party, and the opinions were separated and did not cooperate with each other. The martyr was worried about it, and rushed to write to mediate, and raised tens of thousands of yuan in cash to set up an agency to cooperate with the two factions. At that time, the anti-Li movement in Min was not successful due to other relations, but the comrades were still able to work together in harmony, and united to proceed, which was the reason why the martyr had a broad mind and sincerity. The British governor of Singapore heard of the martyr's name and was very jealous. Because the martyr worked hard on the revolution in his country, his policy of dominating the colony would be adversely affected. The martyr was summoned to inquire about his actions and warned not to, otherwise he would leave the country. The martyr debated in court, eloquently, and the British governor could not be difficult, but he was also very afraid of him. When the dispute over the education regulations of the Malay Archipelago arose, the British officials accused the martyr of resisting the regulations and then Chen Minqing

He was arrested and transferred to Singapore, where he was jailed for two months and deported. After the martyr returned to China, he shifted his spirit and brainpower to promote the development of Fujian, and saw that his hometown was dominated by local tyrants, bandits were everywhere, education was not prosperous, and industry was not prosperous. Wang and others initiated the Heshan United Association, and the He people celebrated their foreheads. Unexpectedly, a group of local tyrants colluded with the Xiamen officials and had unfavorable news for the martyr. The martyr thought that the matter was impossible, so he went to Shanghai and discussed with his comrades in the south to overthrow Li, and took the initiative to raise funds, and went to Siam to open the Rijin Rice Mill, and supervised his younger brother Minqing and others to open a rubber garden and colonize financial resources, in order to prepare to serve the country. At the beginning of the business, it happened that the Eastern Route Crusade Army entered Fujian, the Self-Government Army entered Quanzhou Province, Governor Lin Sen, and sent repeated telegrams to the martyr to return to the country to assist in politics, so he drummed the wheels and returned to the country, arrived in Xiamen, the Minnan militia leaders, and the military and political circles in the provincial capital, and Xiamen agencies and social groups, welcomed Jiang Gan, and discussed major plans together. Governor Lin said that the martyr worked hard in the revolution and was believed by people at home and abroad, and repeatedly asked the martyr to be the chief of the Fujian Finance Department. The leaders of the Minnan militia also repeatedly asked him to be the chief of the Minnan Finance Department. The martyr agreed to do his best to help, but did not hold any name. Soon, the Minnan Martyrdom Comrades Memorial Meeting was initiated. Military and political circles publicly elected the martyr as the chairman, and Xu Ruwei, He Chengjun, Zhang Zhen, and others attended the meeting to express their condolences. Before long, he was ordered to go to Nanyang to raise funds, trek across the ocean, run and shout, his body and mind were exhausted, and he promoted party affairs and lectured everywhere, and his body was unable to support it. When he arrived in Siam, he fell ill and could not get up. It was the 13th of September in the 13th year of the Republic of China, and he was only forty-four years old. The martyr's physique was majestic, and it seemed that the forty-four years of the sun and the moon could not end his life. According to the doctor, the martyr's illness was an internal injury, and the root of the disease was latent when he was jailed in Singapore. Therefore, it is not impossible to ask the British imperialism to kill the martyr. On the day of his funeral, thousands of Chinese and foreign merchants sent him off, some came from thousands of miles away, and each port in Rangoon, Penang, and Xiamen Heshan held an extremely sad memorial service. Four years later, the National Government established its capital in Nanjing and unified the country, commending the martyr. The central government said that the martyr had devoted himself to the party, and gave him a pension at the end, and it was appropriate to build a monument to commemorate him. He ordered the Fujian Provincial Party Department to cooperate with the Provincial Government to be responsible for building the Chen Xinzheng Memorial Stele in Xiamen Zhongshan Park. In the future, the completion of the memorial stele will not only commemorate the martyr, but also encourage the comers. The martyr's old mother is still alive, his wife is Lin, his younger brother is Minqing, Minzhi, and Minyi, and there are one sister each, four sons, and seven daughters. His younger brother Minqing joined the Tongmenghui with the martyr and followed his brother to work hard in the revolutionary cause. After the martyr passed away, Minqing continued his brother's will, enthusiastic and promising, and responded to all public welfare undertakings at home and abroad. In the Northern Expedition and the Jinan case, he initiated the Wounded Soldiers and Refugees Relief Committee with his comrades in Penang, and coordinated with his comrades to do his best to solicit donations, totaling more than one million yuan to the National Government, all of which was the work of the martyr's influence.

Unfortunate Events in the Shipping Industry 121

A series of unfortunate events have befallen ships operating in the Yangtze River. Following the grounding of the Jiejiang-owned "Yibin" which was towed back to Shanghai for repairs, the "Yijiang," also known as "Jiejiang No. 2," which regularly travels between Yichang and Shashi to Shanghai, carrying a substantial amount of cargo, suffered a sudden steam pipe burst mid-journey. Initially unnoticed, upon reaching Jiujiang, the ship’s movement became sluggish. Inspection of the cargo hold by crew members revealed a crack in the hull caused by the steam pipe explosion, allowing river water to flood the compartment. This resulted in significant damage to the cargo. The ship urgently returned to Shanghai to unload the cargo and repair the steam pipe and the damaged hull. Upon inspection, over two hundred bales of cotton shipped from Shashi by Huachang were found to be soaked, resulting in substantial losses. An appraiser has assessed the damage, and a claim for compensation is being negotiated with the shipping company.

Relatives of the "Tongan" Victims Seek Compensation Following the sinking of the Zhaoxing Company’s "Tongan" by the company’s "Lianxing" near Chengshan Bay, resulting in the drowning of many passengers, bereaved families have formed a petition group. They have elected Tian Xingwu and Wang Jiusi as representatives to seek compensation from the company for the deceased. The representatives, noting the proximity of the accident site to Qingdao, first petitioned the Qingdao branch of Zhaoxing. The Qingdao manager, lacking the authority to handle the matter, forwarded the petition to the Shanghai head office for review. The bereaved families have also sent a letter to the Shanghai office requesting compensation of six hundred yuan per person, mirroring the compensation given to the families of workers who died in a Qingdao tobacco factory fire. The Shanghai office has not yet responded to this request.

The "New Yunnan" Reduced to an Empty Shell The saga of the "New Yunnan," which was seized and robbed in Diaoguan, has been previously reported in this newspaper. Further news indicates that after the vessel was initially looted and the crew kidnapped by bandits, the ship remained stranded in Diaoguan. Subsequently, bandits dismantled and looted the interior fittings, passenger accommodations, and deck fixtures. The vessel has now been stripped bare, and the machinery, doors, and other items have been removed. The ship has become a complete write-off. The total loss, including cargo, is estimated at around one million yuan. Compensation for Ship and Cargo Losses Following the grounding of the Taikoo Company's "Jintang" at Chenglingji, over two hundred bales of cotton yarn were abandoned due to bandit threats. The cargo was being transported from Shanghai to Yichang. The consignees have submitted claims for losses to Taikoo, which has agreed to reimburse them at the original cargo value. Furthermore, a large shipment of tobacco leaves transported from Hankou to Shanghai by the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company (CMSNC) was subject to considerable theft upon arrival in Shanghai. The company has investigated on behalf of the clients and apprehended the thieves. To maintain its reputation and protect the clients' investment, the CMSNC will not only severely punish the thieves but also compensate for the missing goods at the market price.

Implementing the Gregorian Calendar for Account Settlement

Yangtze River Passenger Guild Halts Cargo Services 122

The Current State of Chinese Steamships After Resuming Service

A Sharp Decline in Upriver and Downriver Cargo

Chinese steamships on the Yangtze River resumed scheduled services this month after the completion of military transport duties, with each company aggressively trying to break the foreign monopoly and reclaim long-lost shipping rights. However, with the end of the Gregorian calendar year approaching and the implementation of the Gregorian calendar leading to the abolition of the lunar calendar, the passenger guild, due to financial considerations, has suspended cargo services, which has affected Yangtze River shipping. The current situation is detailed below:

Chinese Steamships that Have Resumed Service Among the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company (CMSNC) vessels that have resumed service are the "Jianghua," "Jiangshun," "Jiang’an," "Jiangda," "Jiangyu," "Jiangjing," and "Jianguo" – a total of seven ships. The Sanbei Company has resumed service with the "Changxing," "Chang’an," "Xin Ningxing," and "Guangxing." Zhaoxing has the "Yuxing" and "Zhaoxing," while Ningshao has the "Lao Ningshao."

Request to Release Temporarily Requisitioned Chinese Vessels This time, due to the Chairman's campaign to suppress bandits in Jiangxi, Hubei, and Hunan, the "Jiangtian," "Jiangxin," "Kuaili," "Xingshi," "Yongxing," "Fulong," "Fengpu," and "Dexing" were temporarily requisitioned, and are expected to be released as soon as the anti-bandit troops arrive. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company (CMSNC) has requested the release of the "Si Jiang Xin Kuaili" and has been granted permission. The other vessels will also be released successively.

Lack of Chinese Steamships on the Middle Yangtze River On the middle Yangtze, the sector around Yichang, there are fifteen or sixteen British, Japanese, and American ships, while there is only one Chinese ship, the "Kuaili," which is currently out of service. Passengers in Yichang and Shashi have telegraphed Shanghai shipping companies requesting more ships to meet demand. The Sanbei Company rapidly completed the "Hongli" and dispatched her yesterday as the first Chinese ship to sail directly to Yichang from Shanghai. Due to a shortage of ships, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company (CMSNC) has temporarily dispatched four iron barges between Shanghai and Yichang. Changsha Cargo Piles Up, Ships Requested Chinese shipping in Changsha has been dormant for a long time. Last month, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company (CMSNC) dispatched the "Liyuan" and "Liji" to open the route. It is convenient to load goods for Xiang at Shanghai on Mondays and Thursdays, connecting in Hankou, according to the Xiang guild. Now, because the Xiang River water level has fallen to five feet six inches, and there is a large shipment of rice and cotton from Hunan to Shanghai, telegrams have been sent urging ships to be sent. Sanbei and China Merchants have both transferred shallow-water barges to load. Sanbei has also decided to dispatch the new "Hongzhen" on a direct Shanghai-Xiangsha route from January.

Sharp Decline in Export Business With the implementation of the Gregorian calendar for accounting this year, the Yangtze River passenger guild has stopped issuing loans because the silver houses have stopped lending. Shanghai merchants also require cash for goods, so in the last ten days, outbound cargo on the Yangtze has ceased, and export business has declined sharply. Foreign companies such as Nisshin, Taikoo, and Jardine, which have transshipment cargo, are only loading three or four tenths of a load, even less for Chinese ships. Yesterday, the "Changxing" of Sanbei and the "Ningshao" of Ningshao, heading to Hankou, only carried six or seven hundred taels of cargo each, which was not even enough to cover the cost of coal. There is little hope for Yangtze River business this year, and there is also a severe shortage of cargo coming to Shanghai.

Report on a Major Loan to the Cuban Sugar Consortium 125

A Reuters report from Shanghai on the 11th states that there are rumours from Nanjing that a major Cuban sugar consortium is in talks with the Chinese authorities to invest between 300 million and 500 million US dollars in Chinese industries. It is said that the Cuban sugar consortium is most interested in China's sugar monopoly and road construction. However, these rumours have not been officially confirmed. A Mr. Pei Laitai, said to be a South American capitalist, recently visited the new capital with two legal advisors and several Chinese assistants. During his meeting with the Chinese government authorities, Mr. Pei Laitai proposed that the Cuban sugar industry invest 20 million US dollars to develop China's sugar industry and urged the National Government to actively adopt this plan. All raw sugar imported from Cuba into China would be exempt from taxes, and the Cuban sugar consortium would share profits equally with the Chinese government, with the Cuban sugar consortium enjoying a 20-year monopoly on the Chinese sugar market. At the end of the 20-year period, the National Government would be able to take over its assets and interests in China and be compensated. However, the Chinese authorities rejected this proposal because China imports approximately 100 million taels of silver worth of sugar annually, and the government collects approximately 15 million yuan in sugar taxes each year. The Cuban sugar consortium's plan is unlikely to increase the Chinese government's revenue. The sugar consortium then greatly changed its conditions, rumoured to be willing to invest 20 million US dollars specifically for Chinese sugar production. Cuban sugar imports would still be subject to taxation, and there would be no monopoly in China. However, the Cuban sugar consortium would receive five percent of the profits from this business. It is said that the contract has not yet been agreed upon, and the negotiations are still in the initial stages. Mr. Pei Laitai is currently collecting information from the Ministry of Railways regarding highway and railway development. According to him, although the Cuban sugar consortium was originally focused on developing China's sugar industry, it also plans to invest tens of millions of US dollars in Chinese construction projects.

Japanese Business

A Glimpse of the Economic Downturn 126

Published by the Japanese Commercial Office in Shanghai

Import Surplus for the First Eleven Months of This Year

The Japanese Commercial Counselor in Shanghai received an official telegram from Tokyo on December 11th, stating that the total value of Japan's foreign trade import and export from January to November this year reached 2,800,000,000 yen, with an import surplus of 93,000,000 yen. This is an increase of 25,000,000 yen compared to the import surplus for the same period last year. The main exports were raw silk, silk textiles, and cotton textiles, totaling 670,000,000 yen. Compared to the same period last year, raw silk and silk products decreased by 50%, and cotton textiles decreased by 34%. The main imports were raw cotton, iron, machinery, wool, and timber, all of which decreased compared to the same period last year. During these eleven months, Japan's export trade to China was worth 369,000,000 yen, with an export surplus of 110,000,000 yen, a decrease of 50,000,000 yen compared to the export surplus for the same period last year. Looking at the overall commercial situation this year, the phenomenon of the economic downturn in Japan is evident. The budget for 1931 has been set at 1,448,000,000 yen, a decrease of 160,000,000 yen compared to last year. The government is currently discussing reducing the tax burden on the people and using relief bonds and funds saved from the London Naval Treaty to make up for it.

Various Sectors in the Yinxiang District

Preparing to Celebrate New Year's Day 127

The Seventh District, Eleventh Branch, Twelfth Branch, and Sanyou Labor Union of this city convened a meeting of various organizations and groups in the Yinxiang District at the Sanyou Labor Union at 3:00 PM on the 11th of this month to organize the Yinxiang District New Year’s Day Celebration Preparatory Committee. Attendees included the Sanyou Labor Union, the Eleventh and Twelfth Branches, the Sanyou Industrial Society, the Minyou Consumer Cooperative, the Minyou Drama Society, the Fifth District Fourth Precinct, the Yinxiang District Teachers’ Association, the Commercial Federation, and the Yinxi Elementary School. Lu Xiang presided, and the ritual was performed. After the chairman's report, discussions began on (1) determining the name of the preparatory committee, which was resolved to be named the "Shanghai Yinxiang District All Circles New Year’s Day Celebration Preparatory Committee"; (2) how the preparatory committee should be organized, with a resolution to establish a General Affairs Department, a Propaganda Department, and a Entertainment Department. The General Affairs Department would have a Document Section, an Economic Section, a General Affairs Section, a Inspection Section, and a Communication Section. The Propaganda Department would have a Speech Section, an Editorial Section, and an Expanded Propaganda Section. The duties of each section were allocated as follows: Documents (Twelfth Branch), Economics (Minyou Cooperative), General Affairs (Sanyou Labor Union), Communication (Sanyou Labor Union), Inspection (Fifth District Fourth Precinct), Speech (Eleventh Branch), Editing (Twelfth Branch), Expanded Propaganda (Eleventh Branch); (6) where the location of this association should be, with a resolution that the office should be located inside the Sanyou Labor Union, and the venue should be the large playground outside the Beizha; and (7) how to regulate the date and time of the association's office, with a resolution that from now on, a meeting would be held every three days (convened by the General Affairs Department) from 4:00 PM to 5:00 PM.

Confession of Anti-British Indian 129

Leaflets Distributed the Day Before Yesterday

Eloquent Speech Yesterday

The Great American Evening News reports that the British Police Court opened the trial of Indian Su Yangxin this morning (12th) on charges of distributing seditious writings. Su gave an eloquent speech in court, claiming that he would rather be imprisoned than enjoy freedom under British rule. Although his actions were to appeal for the rights of himself and his compatriots, he did not expect the benevolence of the British government. After he joined the army in 1918, he had received the government's favour, and at that time, the government promised autonomy to the Indians, ordered the Indians to wish for the victory of the British army, and when the war ended, martial law was declared in India, and taxes were levied, even on weddings. Today, we appeal for our inherent rights, and are called seditious. If the British government does not abandon India, we Indians are willing to drive them out by force. After the defendant finished his statement, the questioner told him that this kind of speech was useless to him, the preliminary hearing had already been established, and he was to be sent to the High Court for interrogation. The defendant was accused of being detained on the 11th for distributing reactionary leaflets at the intersection of North Henan Road and Tiantong Road.

A Sudden Fire at the Si Hai Sheng Ping Lou Last Night 130

Burned for an Hour

Stores Downstairs Were Affected

Cause of Fire Still Unknown

Large Losses Suffered by Each Business

At 7:55 PM last night, a sudden fire broke out at the Si Hai Sheng Ping Lou on Fuzhou Road. It took an hour to extinguish, and the losses were quite large. The details are recorded below.

The famous tea house Si Hai Sheng Ping Lou, located at M153-154 Fuzhou Road, is one of the most well-known tea houses in Shanghai, comparable in business to Qing Lian Ge. The upper floor occupies eleven rooms, extending from the East Huitong Fang alley to the West Huitong Fang alley. At 7:55 PM last night, a fire suddenly broke out in the back of the building, and smoke filled the surrounding area.

Traffic Interrupted The Central Fire Brigade rushed to the scene upon receiving the alarm. In addition to a pumper truck parked in Huitong Fang alley on Sanma Road to prevent the spread, the remaining vehicles were all driven to the fire scene. The number 21 pumper truck was used to draw water and spray, and traffic was immediately cut off. In addition to the 17-trolley buses being stuck at the Shandong Road intersection and the Shilu intersection, all other vehicles were detoured.

Store Losses When the fire was raging and the firefighters were bravely fighting the fire, all the stores under the tea house suffered losses, extending westward from the East Huitong Fang alley. These included the Yongzai Electrical Appliance Company at 150-151, the Xu Shengji Picture Postcard Distributor at 152, the Qunxue Bookstore at 155, the Baixin Company Bookstore at 156, the Jinwentang Bookstore at 157, and, to the west, the West Huitong Fang alley.

Unknown Cause The fire was at its worst at 8:20 PM, and more hoses were added to suppress it. The fire was slightly reduced until 8:50 PM, and it was completely extinguished at 9:10 PM. It is said that the losses from this incident were quite large, but all were insured. The cause of the fire is unknown.

Dong Kang Does Not Approve

Dong Yu's Divorce 131

Letter to the Civil Court President of the French Concession

Stating the Origins of Dong Yu's Marriage

Cannot Be Abused by Inappropriately Applying Disability

Dong Kang wrote to the Civil Court President of the French Concession on behalf of his client, Dong Yu, in a divorce case with his wife, Ms. Jiang, stating that the Court President, Dong Jingxi, namely Dong Yu, has filed a suit to divorce his wife, Ms. Jiang. The court heard the case on the 3rd of this month and ordered that a reconciliation be attempted within two weeks. Now, I have received a summons to continue the hearing on the 11th. Kang, as a witness in this case, should state the facts of the case to your Honour. Dong Yu is a relative of Kang. Kang recommended him as a clerk in the Jiangsu and Shandong High Courts. In the tenth year of the Republic, Kang was asked to introduce him to Ms. Jiang Youzhi, the great-granddaughter of Jiang Renjing of Anhui, as his wife. Initially, one matchmaker was Mr. Chen (Ms. Jiang's brother-in-law) and the other was Fan Zhaochang. The betrothal was made at Kang's residence. In the winter of that year, it was rumoured that Dong Yu had formally married Ms. Lu, the daughter of Lu Zhipeng of Haimen, in Shandong. At that time, Kang was the Minister of Justice and telegraphed him to Beijing, advising him to cancel the marriage contract with Ms. Jiang to avoid future complications. Dong Yu insisted that the status of his wife and concubine was no different, and there would be no disagreement. In the eleventh year, Kang was sent to travel in Europe and the United States. In that year, Dong Yu used Kang's name as the wedding officiant to hold the wedding with Ms. Jiang in Shanghai. They lived together for a year and had a daughter. Because the treatment was not equal, she often lived with her mother and relatives. Last year, after persuasion from relatives and friends, they reunited and welcomed Ms. Jiang home again. In October of this year, Ms. Lu died of measles. Dong Yu asked his cousin, Ms. He Dong, to suggest to Ms. Jiang that they divorce. Ms. Jiang did not agree. Afterwards, she personally visited Kang and repeated her previous statement. Kang believed that the divorce proposal was strange because it was made after Ms. Lu's death, not before, and strongly advised against it. Unexpectedly, Dong Yu then requested a divorce from Ms. Jiang in your court, claiming that she had a long-standing liver disease and citing precedents from the Dali Yuan to support his claim. An investigation into marriage between men and women reveals that prior notice must be given in the case of disabilities. The effective part of the penal code in the preceding Qing dynasty recognizes, the law originated from Tang Code and Annotated Commentary, says, status should be three disease, body not intact, three disease is severe illness, disability and chronic illness is total name. Cannot work because of severe disability, body not intact, hidden disease is sky eunuch, women cannot birth, body not intact. Based on annotations, do not abuse. Kang was in the Imperial Judiciary for four terms, a total of eight years, and the issued judgements were verified. There is no precedent like this. Moreover, Ms. Jiang is usually healthy, and it has not been heard that she has any disease. Kang recently ordered Dong Yu to go home and persuaded him to follow the order to mediate. Dong Yu prepared a divorce contract, roughly in the name of a deposit of three thousand yuan, giving Ms. Jiang eight percent interest per month. At the end, it also stated that the man and woman's marriage should not interfere with each other. Ms. Jiang also agreed that the couple should live separately and set conditions. If it is said that she was abandoned, she only knows to follow one person to the end, and she is not happy to hear anything else. Kang happened to be going to Yu for business, and he did not know what happened to the negotiations after that. I think that Your Honour is clear-minded and will see the slightest flaw. Ms. Jiang comes from a large family and has encountered such a situation, which is not without pity. The purpose she holds is not without the virtue of a woman. I still ask for a time limit to try to reconcile. If it is not compatible, I can only wait for Your Honour to judge according to the law. Kang originally intended to go to court to make a statement today, but he returned from Yu yesterday and felt ill on the way, so he entrusted Lawyer Wang to convey his message. I hope you will take note of this. Yours respectfully, Dong Kang, the tenth day.

Fake Warehouse Receipt

Cheated More Than 10,000 Gold 132

Wing Hang Bank Sues Xu Xiangfu et al.

Defrauded a Large Amount of Money Twice with Fake Warehouse Receipts

Wing Hang Bank, located at 196 Ningbo Road, was recently defrauded of 10,467.8 taels of silver with fake warehouse receipts by Xu Xiangfu and others from Zhejiang. After the bank discovered the fraud, it reported it to the General Police Station, which sent Detective Wu Chunrong to arrest Xu and hand him over to the Special District Local Court for questioning. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhou Hanting opened the court to question him. Ruyi Bao, the lawyer of the police station, stated the circumstances of the defendant's deception, saying that the defendant, Xu Xiangfu, was the accountant of Shengfeng Yarn and Cotton Company at 510 Tianjin Road. Shengfeng had business dealings with Wing Hang since March this year, and its credit was still good. On the 1st of this month, Cai Qingzhang, a Wing Hang broker, brought two warehouse receipts from Shengfeng, one for 130 bales of cotton and the other for 170 bales of cotton. The goods were stored in the Nanshi Dachu Company. He wanted to mortgage them for 3,622.86 taels of silver. Wing Hang did not suspect it was fake and accepted the mortgage, paying two bills, one for 2,972.86 taels and the other for 650 taels. On the 5th of this month, Cai brought three warehouse receipts for 487 bales of cotton and mortgaged them to Wing Hang for 6,845 taels of silver. The mortgagor and the storage location were the same as before. The bank also accepted them and paid them all in promissory notes. The next day, Wing Hang, for the sake of caution, sent shop assistant Li Afu to Shengfeng with the warehouse receipts to inquire. The defendant Xu Xiangfu was at the store and, in addition to verbally acknowledging it, stamped the Shengfeng seal on the warehouse receipts to strengthen Wing Hang's trust. The bank then sent Zhang Quanfu to inquire with Dachu Company about the warehouse receipts. Dachu told him that Shengfeng had no goods stored there, and the warehouse receipts were not issued by Dachu. Zhang reported the situation to the bank manager, who then sent Vice President Sun Xueqiao to Shengfeng to ask Xu. Xu claimed that the warehouse receipts belonged to Xu Hao, the owner of Shengfeng, and that he did not know the truth. Sun felt that Xu Xiangfu's words were vague and reported him to the police station. He denied being the accountant of Shengfeng and said that he was the small owner of Yongxinglong Customs Broker. After the police station detained the defendant, detailed investigations revealed that the address of Shengfeng was actually the address of Yongxinglong Customs Broker, and Shengfeng was only a sign hanging at the door, with no other equipment. Therefore, the two firms were actually one and the same. Later, it was heard that Xu Hao lived at 19 Baoshan Road. When detectives were sent to arrest him, he had already escaped in advance. As for the promissory notes paid by Wing Hang twice, the one for 650 taels had already been deposited in the Zhengxiang Qianzhuang on Doushi Street in Nanshi. Of the four notes given the second time, the defendant deposited two notes of 2,250 taels and 1,300 taels in the name of Yongxinglong into the Tongan Qianzhuang at 364 Henan Road, but then withdrew them, and Tongan gave him banknotes. The remaining two notes were initially deposited in the Tongji Qianzhuang at 250 Tianjin Road, because Yongxinglong also had dealings with Tongxing and owed Tongxing money, so they could not be withdrawn immediately. Later, because the situation was urgent and Wing Hang's note had not yet expired, they were taken back from Tong'an Qianzhuang, and Xu Hao took them away. According to Qianzhuang regulations, this kind of note is no different from cash. It should be requested to issue a ticket to quickly bring Xu Hao and Cai Qingzhang to the case. Then, Sun Xueqiao proved that the defrauding process was similar to the lawyer's statement. Judge Zhou asked Xu Xiangfu, and Xu completely blamed the matter on Xu Hao alone. The judge ordered him to hand over Xu Hao to the case as soon as possible, otherwise, he would be held responsible. The case was adjourned for seven days for hearing.

Hat Lost, Left Ear Run Over 134

Life Possibly in Danger

Xu Laifa, a man from Hangzhou, around thirty years old, boarded the Shanghai-Songhu passenger train from Shanghai at approximately 2 PM yesterday. He intended to visit a friend surnamed He at a certain school in Baotaiwan. After the train stopped at the Wusong Town station, the melon-rind satin hat Xu was wearing suddenly fell out the window. The driver immediately stopped the train. The stationmaster ordered a porter to help Xu up. He was bleeding profusely, and his face was a bloody mess, a terrible sight. Inspecting Passengers in the First and Second Halves of the Night 136

Special Order During the Winter Defense Period

Yuan, the director of the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau, recently considered the importance of winter defense. In addition to issuing orders to the subordinate district offices to increase the number of patrol officers and organize patrol teams to patrol all night, he also sent police squad leaders and officers to be stationed in the jurisdictions of each district office to assist in protection. Considering that hotels and inns are most prone to harboring bandits, inspections cannot be relaxed in the slightest. If suspicious travelers are encountered, they should be questioned in detail about their origins and destinations to prevent evildoers from hiding within the territory and to maintain public security.

Hanukkah Dance Party 137

Initiated by the Hebron Church

Held on the Evening of the 17th

The local Hebron Church will hold a Hanukkah dance party at the Grand Hua Hotel on the evening of the 17th. Hanukkah is an ancient Jewish holiday. In the past, pagans invaded Palestine. The famous Jewish general Maccabees fought and defeated the invaders, and the Jewish state was preserved. This battle was crucial to the fate of the Jewish state and the survival of its religion. Therefore, Jewish people attach great importance to it and regard the day of victory as a major holiday of the year. The local Hebron Church often holds dance parties on this day. The program is very grand and is considered the best for the time being. The proceeds from ticket sales will be allocated to the Jewish National Fund and the local Jewish Education Assistance Association's expenses.

The Lusida sandboat Gu Fa Shun was loaded with more than 700 dan of red dates from Jiaozhou to Shanghai for unloading. Zhao Di Unwilling to Engage in a Life of Prostitution 140

Escaped Back to Her Mother's Home in Pudong

Madam Still Attempting to Recover Her

Geng Yao, a woman from Rugao, forty-three years old, lives at No. 18 Diandang Lane, Lannidu, Pudong. Her husband, Geng, died of illness last summer. She has no children. She has a daughter, twenty-five years old, who is already married. There is an adopted daughter, Zhao Di, who is sixteen years old, with a beautiful face and clever intelligence, still unmarried. Since her husband's death, Yao's family has fallen into decline, with debts piling up, unable to cope. Unable to do otherwise, on July 2nd of the lunar calendar this year, she pawned Zhao Di into the Wei surname brothel, No. 1 Tongzhi Lane, near Baxianqiao in the French Concession, to be a prostitute. Ren Wang and others acted as intermediaries, agreeing on a pawn price of seventy yuan, for a term of six months. Both the people and money were handed over immediately. Because Zhao Di was young and beautiful, customers flocked to her as soon as she entered the brothel. The Madam saw that the prostitution business was booming and regarded Zhao Di as a cash cow. However, Zhao Di catered to customers day and night, unable to bear the suffering. Two weeks ago, she escaped from the fiery pit and sneaked back to her mother's home in Pudong. The former intermediary Ren Wang was sent to Pudong to negotiate with Zhao Di's mother, Yao. Yao was willing to return the pawn price of seventy yuan, but Ren said that the Madam wanted 192 yuan before the pawn contract could be handed over; otherwise, Zhao Di would still have to go to make up the date. As soon as Zhao Di heard this, her heart was on fire. She went to the No. 3 District of the Public Security Bureau to report for assistance. The District Chief immediately ordered a patrol officer to go with her and bring Ren Wang and Zhao Di's mother, Yao, to the district. According to Geng Yao's statement, her daughter Zhao Di was adopted at the age of three and treated as her own. In fact, after her husband's death, she owed funeral expenses and was forced to pawn her into the brothel, receiving a price of seventy yuan, deducting expenses, and netting sixty-three yuan. Now she is willing to return the pawn price and take her back to marry someone else. Please investigate. Zhao Di testified that she had been prostituting for more than two months since her mother pawned her into the brothel, earning more than ten yuan a night if she was lucky, and no less than five or six yuan if she was not. She has earned more than 300 yuan in total, but the suffering is unbearable. She vows that she is unwilling to engage in a life of prostitution and requests assistance. Ren Wang testified that she was thirty-seven years old, from Sanjiang, and lived at No. 10 Huangpu Road, Datiebang. There were four people in total, including herself, who acted as intermediaries for Zhao Di. Now Zhao Di escaped before the term was up. The brothel was asking her for the person, so she came to Pudong to look for her, etc. The District Chief considered that this case involved social morality and humanity and ruled that the people involved would be transferred to the

Public Security Bureau Headquarters yesterday with a document for further investigation.

A Fast-Moving Truck Injured a Person 142

At approximately 4:10 PM yesterday afternoon, in the middle of Jisevier Road in Caojiadu, western Shanghai, a truck with Concession License No. 9556 and Chinese License No. 8325 was speeding from east to west. Accidentally, it crashed heavily into a small cart loaded with planks, knocking both the cart driver and the cart to the ground. The cart driver was pinned under the cart, his head bleeding, and his feet and other places were also injured. The guard saw this and stepped forward to help the injured person and take the truck and driver back to the No. 6 District Police Station. The police were immediately dispatched to send the injured person to the hospital for treatment, pending investigation.

Woman Fell From the Drying Platform and Injured Herself 143

At half past noon yesterday, Wang, the wife of Jin Renbin, a man from Pudong who lived in the pavilion room of the Bao Kang Zhuang soy sauce garden at No. 37 Xie Xu Road, Nanshi, fell from the drying platform and was seriously injured. She was taken to Shanghai Hospital by a guard for treatment.

Female Star Tang Xueqian Returns 144

Reconciled with Fei Manqian as Before

Tang Xueqian, the wife of Fei Manqian, a movie star, disappeared suddenly after an argument with her husband. She has now been found, and the two have reconciled as before. The details are recorded below. Fei Manqian, from Zhejiang, worked in the newspaper industry. Later, he co-edited publications with Xu Zhimo, Yang Qingyin, and others at the National Art Exhibition Preparatory Office of the Ministry of Education. His writings have appeared in various newspapers and magazines. Three years ago, he and his wife Tang Xueqian worked as actors at the Xifan Film Company. Later, Fei took on other work and served as a screenwriter at the Ruilong Film Company, Jincheng, and Five Star Film Company. Ms. Tang Xueqian, from Shandong, followed her father to Shanghai when she was young. Her father was a maritime tycoon. Because she was skilled in martial arts, she served as the director of the women's division of the Jingwu Athletic Association. She loved Peking Opera and performed on stage to great acclaim. She also studied painting with the famous painter Yang Qingyin. Their marriage was difficult because Tang's mother did not approve, but they finally achieved their goal. Last spring, they had a son named Qingbai, who is unusually strong. This summer, they had another daughter. They are very interested in family life. It is conceivable that they respect and love each other since they have achieved such happiness. Therefore, they have been married for three years without any quarrels and are exceptionally harmonious. On the evening of the 9th, there was a misunderstanding over a trivial matter, which led to an argument. On the morning of the 10th, Tang went out alone, resulting in yesterday's news. Fortunately, Fei sent out scouts and was able to rescue her. Now, with the mediation of friends, they have reconciled.

Free Love Starts Well, Ends with Abandonment 145

Zhang Juqing, a woman from Ningbo, twenty-two years old, loved freedom and fell in love with Wan Bingzhong, who worked at Lao Deji Pharmacy, in June three years ago. On the 21st of the same month, Wan seduced her to open a room at the Jiangnan Hotel and, after a free engagement, engaged in cohabitation. She became pregnant for seven months. Unexpectedly, Wan abandoned the old for the new and, after getting acquainted with another woman, falsely claimed in May of this year that his business was suspended and that he planned to go to Nanjing to find work. Since then, he abandoned Juqing and never met again. Later, Juqing met Wan's friend Feng on the road and learned that Wan was still in Shanghai, so she went to find him. Unexpectedly, Wan said that she was not worthy to be his wife. Juqing was extremely angry and took Wan Bingzhong to the No. 2 District No. 2 Branch a few days ago. Because the case concerned a marital dispute, it was transferred to the Public Security Bureau for investigation. After investigation, the Public Security Bureau found that free love was a civil matter and ordered her to file a lawsuit in court. At that time, Juqing said that Wan Bingzhong was actually guilty of abduction, rape, and abandonment and demanded severe punishment. Because abduction and rape are private prosecution crimes, they should be prosecuted by the parents. She was still ordered to file a lawsuit in court. Yesterday (the 12th) at 8 AM, Zhang Juqing's biological mother, Zhang Dong, heard that her daughter had been abducted, raped, and abandoned, and that she was pregnant. Now Wan abandoned her without any concern, which she could not bear. She took Juqing to Wan Bingzhong's residence (No. 90 Yangjiafangchang) to question Wan and made a big fuss. Unexpectedly, Wan was unreasonable. She called Wang Xuehe, a guard from the No. 2 District No. 1 Branch No. 28 Post, who brought the people and witnesses to the station. After interrogation by Director Qian, it was found that Wan Bingzhong had committed abduction, rape, and abandonment against Zhang Juqing. It was ordered that he be sent to the Public Security Bureau Headquarters for legal action.

Liu Ji Er Crushed to Death by a Cotton Bale 146

Liu A'er, a man from Jiangbei, around fifty years old, had been a porter at the Dasheng Wharf warehouse in Nanshi. At 9 AM yesterday, he and his nephew Liu Guangfa were carrying a bale of cotton to the ship. When walking on the gangway, he was weak and lost his footing and fell. Both of them fell to the ground, but the nephew was spared injury. Liu Er was crushed on the head by the cotton, his brains flowed out, and he died on the spot. Lu Yongde, the local head of the 16th Shop, reported to the Local Court. Prosecutor Lei and others arrived at the scene to investigate and ordered the family to collect the body.

Financial management and administration are for the benefit of the country. He followed the law and simplified punishments to protect the people. In this age of decline, we are fortunate to admire the great man. He is a guide to ethics and a model for all ages. Why was He Wu Yang summoned so quickly? He flew high on a crane. From now on, where will we place our trust? The vast sky has broken our pillar. Tracing his appearance and voice, where can we find them? We cannot bear to look at the flying white banner. Publication of the Shanghai Financial History Supplement 152

Mr. Xu Jiqin of Yongjia wrote the book "Recent Shanghai Financial History" in the fifteenth year of the Republic of China. Later, in the spring of the eighteenth year, it was revised and republished, and the content became more abundant. Since its publication, it has been popular at home and abroad and can be praised as the needle of the south in the financial world. This year, in order to supplement the financial materials of the past two years, the author has compiled two supplements. One is devoted to the business reports of various Chinese and foreign banks, trust companies, and savings associations in Shanghai in the seventeenth year of the Republic of China. The second is devoted to the business reports and survey tables of various Chinese and foreign banks, trust companies, savings associations, and money shops in Shanghai in the eighteenth year of the Republic of China. The two supplements were published in February and November of this year, respectively. Each volume has more than 100 pages. The content focuses on figures and does not emphasize empty talk. Those who want to explore the situation of the Shanghai financial world in the past two years must have a copy. It is said that the supplements are sold together with the revised financial history and are still priced at one yuan and five dimes, with no additional charge. The consignment locations are the Shanghai and various Commercial Press bookstores and the Shanghai Banking Weekly Society.

Zhang Fang's Views on Relieving the Henan Disaster 155

Speech at the Welcoming Banquet the Previous Evening

Zhang Fang, member of the Henan Provincial Government and concurrently Director of the Civil Affairs Department, Commander-in-Chief of the 20th Route Army, and Chairman of the Henan Relief Committee, arrived in Shanghai on the morning of the 9th from Beijing. Fellow Henan provincials in Shanghai, Fan Zhengbo and Ren Taoyu, held a welcoming meeting at the East Asia Building at 6:00 PM on the 11th. About two to three hundred Henan natives attended. Chairman Fan Zhengbo delivered a welcoming speech, to which Mr. Zhang responded with extreme humility and concern for his homeland. The measures he proposed were well-organized. His speech is recorded below:

"I am truly unworthy of the welcome extended to me by my fellow provincials today. I bear a responsibility, both publicly and privately, for the relief of Henan. However, in recent months, there has been little improvement in the disaster situation in Henan. I already feel deeply ashamed and dare not accept your welcome. However, I would like to take this opportunity to report on the disaster in Henan and the reasons for my visit to Shanghai. I believe that all of you are concerned about our homeland and will be eager to hear and willing to offer guidance. Henan has always been known as a region of frequent warfare. Over the years, it has suffered from military disasters, as you all know. Since 1920, there have been droughts, floods, locusts, and hailstorms, coupled with the rampant activities of bandits. Ordinary people simply cannot live a decent life. Since the success of the revolution, the people had hoped for a better future. Who would have thought that the recent rebellion instigated by Yan and Feng would focus on Henan? The loss of life and property, both direct and indirect, suffered by the people is incalculable, especially in the forty-eight counties, including Kaifeng and Chenliu. Therefore, I recently petitioned the central government to provide relief through the following measures: (1) establish soup kitchens and shelters for women and children in the aforementioned forty-eight counties; (2) fill in war trenches, repair roads and the Yellow River dike to create jobs; (3) establish grain stabilization bureaus to stabilize grain prices; (4) provide loans of cattle, tools, and seeds to the people to restore cultivation; (5) continue to transport disaster victims to the eastern provinces for settlement and border consolidation. If these five measures can be effectively implemented, at least ten million yuan will be required. If this can be achieved, the disaster victims in Henan may have a glimmer of hope. Recently, the relief efforts in Henan have been greatly assisted by the enthusiastic help of various charitable organizations in Shanghai. The thirty million disaster victims in the province are immensely grateful. Therefore, on behalf of all the disaster victims in the province, I respectfully express my thanks. However, as you philanthropists are scattered in various places, and my time in Shanghai is limited, I am afraid I may not be able to visit all of you. I hope you will understand. In addition, there is one thing I hope all of you present will consider, and that is the issue of self-help. Because the disaster in Henan is too severe, government funding may not be enough to fully save everyone. If you can all unite and appeal to people everywhere to understand the disaster situation in Henan, arouse their benevolence, and generously donate funds, every penny more will bring a penny more of benefit to the disaster victims in Henan. These are my humble opinions, and I ask that you not hesitate to give me your guidance, which I eagerly await day and night." After Mr. Zhang finished his speech, the entire building erupted in thunderous applause. Afterwards, a banquet was held in Mr. Zhang's honor, and the guests and host enjoyed themselves immensely before departing.

Yesterday at noon, Zhang Fang hosted a banquet for people from all walks of life at the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce. Cai Yuanpei, Jiao Yitang, Zhang Yuejun, Wang Yiting, Fan Zhengbo, Pan Gongzhan, Wang Yansong, Xu Jinyuan, Xu Junren, Yuan Liang, Zhang Xiaolin, Du Yuesheng, Yu Qiaqing, Fang Jiaobo, Shang Mujiang, Lü Gongwang, Gu Zhuxuan, Wang Xiaolai, Lu Bohong, Ye Huijun, and over a hundred others attended. During the banquet, Mr. Zhang delivered a speech first, followed by speeches from Cai Yuanpei, Zhang Yuejun, Wang Yiting, and others, all expressing deep sorrow. The guests and host parted on amicable terms around 3:00 PM.

Railway Bureau Remedies for Passenger Train Delays 156

The East Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureau and its Train Operations Department, concerned about passenger complaints due to recent delays in various passenger trains, and in the midst of railway reorganization, could not allow such delays to damage the railway's reputation. Therefore, they convened a meeting of various section chiefs at the bureau the day before yesterday to discuss solutions. It was decided that before the new locomotives were installed, personnel would be dispatched to conduct on-site investigations along the railway line to determine the causes of the delays and take remedial measures. Deputy Director Zheng Huozhao of the Train Operations Department was assigned to be responsible for the investigation, and the Director of the Locomotive Department was instructed to order all drivers to exercise caution and strive to avoid delays. It is learned that Director Zheng Huozhao, after receiving his orders, set off yesterday morning at 6:00 AM on an express train to conduct the investigation. However, according to personnel at the bureau, the delays, in terms of responsibility, should be attributed to the Locomotive Department. The poor quality of the coal purchased by the Purchasing Committee on behalf of the railway is the primary cause. The oil inside the axles also has a significant impact. In the past, the axle oil used could average up to one hundred revolutions before overheating, but the current oil can only withstand about three hundred revolutions before overheating. Occasionally, axles overheat, rendering the trains unusable and causing delays due to the time required for disassembly. Additionally, the arrival of winter causes the heat from the locomotives to be affected by the cold weather, inevitably reducing speed. As for the Train Operations Department, it has exhausted all possible methods to remedy the situation.

Lost Boy Waiting to Be Claimed 166

The Municipal Public Security Bureau reported yesterday that a lost boy, Ma Xiaomao, was sent in by the Second District. He was found in Rihui Port. He claimed to be 11 years old, from Kunshan, living at Xiaoshi Bridge in Kunshan. His father's name is Xin Xiao. His father brought him to Shanghai and left him with his stepmother, who runs a candy store. His father then disappeared. He wandered out on his own and got lost. The boy has ringworm on his head, a round face, wears a floral-patterned cotton robe, gray cotton pants, black socks, and cloth shoes. He is currently being held at the Xin Puyu Tang to await a claimant.

News from Various Native Associations 167

Chongde: Cai Yuan, courtesy name Pin Neng, from Chongde, Zhejiang, has been involved in diplomacy in Shenyang for many years. He came south with Zhang Xueliang this time. Last night, the county native association held a welcoming meeting at Yi Zhi Xiang. Zhou Weiyuan, Dai Luling, Wang Lianfang, Representative Lu Ziquan, and over forty other people attended. Chairman Zhou delivered a welcoming speech first, followed by a speech by Cai Yuan, who also donated a large sum of money. Next, the members subscribed to monthly donations. Then, association affairs were discussed. The public enthusiastically supported the association and hoped for its development. The guests and host parted on amicable terms at midnight.

Xiuning: The Xiuning Native Association in Shanghai will hold a memorial service at 2:00 PM on the afternoon of the 14th at the association's auditorium on Avenue Haig in memory of the first anniversary of the death of Zhu Qiguang, a member of the association's Standing Committee. All members of the association and friends of Zhu Jun are welcome to attend.

Fire on Julida Road 168

A fire broke out unexpectedly at Wang Jinji's coal yard, No. 5, Xinchang Lane, Julida Road, in the French Concession yesterday afternoon at 3:45 PM. The flames quickly spread, like a prairie fire. The yard was filled with coal, firewood, and other goods, all of which were burned to ashes. The fire also spread to the adjacent Tongxing Dyeing Factory, and its silks and fabrics were also destroyed. The French Concession Fire Department's lookout tower saw the fire and immediately rang the alarm. More than ten fire engines arrived, and the firefighters bravely fought the fire. It was not extinguished until about 6:00 PM. It is estimated that three to four houses were destroyed and about five to six thousand yuan worth of goods were lost.

Weather Report 169

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday was: cloudy and relatively clear weather in this area and the Yangtze River basin, with rain or snow around Shandong, and northwest winds or gales. There will be north to northeast winds of varying strength in Ma'anshan Island and the south. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this city was 61.7 degrees and the lowest was 39.0 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest temperature was 63.3 degrees and the lowest was 49.8 degrees.

Letter 170

To the editors of Shen Bao:

I am writing to you concerning the report in the local news column of your December 12 issue, which stated that Deputy Commander Zhang Xueliang's representative, Xu Shiying, sent condolences to Commander Xiong Tianji. I would like to clarify that Mr. Shiying's visit yesterday was purely a personal matter and that he was not entrusted by Deputy Commander Zhang to represent him. I would appreciate it if you could correct the record. Respectfully yours, Xu Shiying, December 12.

Dear Editor,

I am writing to you regarding the news report that Mr. Liu Renqing died of suffocation due to family troubles. According to Mr. Liu Zhao, Mr. Liu Renqing established the Yihe Yong Clock Factory. Mr. Zhao and Mr. Liu have been living together in Shanghai for many years. There has never been a Mrs. Chen. All of the factory's capital was raised by Mr. Zhao and Mr. Liu in their hometown. There are still outstanding debts.

The report contains many errors. It is likely based on hearsay. I request that you correct the record. Sincerely, Liu Zhao, December 12.
