Free Talk

Thoughts 172

— Yi Mei

Flying love bullets. Armor is not enough to resist.

Long trips are lonely. Reading the newspaper at this time is the most comprehensive.

A small shop always posts its market name, saying that it is the world, the globe, or the Far East. This shows the exaggeration of the national character.

All the world's most complex machinery is not enough to match the minds of writers.

If a woman's mysterious door could be moved to her forehead, it would reduce much adultery and wickedness.

Writers are not afraid of writing, but they are afraid of copying. Calligraphers are not afraid of writing, but they are afraid of grinding ink.

When you find a childhood photo, you laugh at first and then feel emotional.

A shelf of books, a window of bamboo, a wall of paintings, a stove of incense, a jug of wine, and a pot of flowers are enough to be called six recluses.

The market price of love has become cheaper and cheaper in recent years. It can be bought with a small amount of gold.

Most rich people are willing to hide beauties in golden houses but are unwilling to shelter scholars in mansions.

We should not look at people with white eyes, nor should we envy people with red eyes.

Closing the door and sweeping away dust, there is joy in this.

The three words "model" are sacred terms in art. If they are called "sensual," then there is contempt.

Reading in the toilet is lewd, but it is interesting.

If you want to urinate on the road, you can seek it from the poisonous door advertisement.

Drawing portraits of ladies, chanting erotic poems, and writing sad novels are most likely to move a woman's heart.

A non-clever person cannot say witty words.

The Western movie star, Lang Qui Nai, has the reputation of having a thousand faces. Unexpectedly, this kind of art is also well performed by our country's dignitaries and politicians.

On One of the First Students Studying Abroad from Pudong 173

— Juemi

In the winter of the tenth year of Tongzhi in the Qing Dynasty, Zeng Wenzhenggong of Xiangxiang, the Nanyang Minister and Governor-General of Liangjiang, commissioned Xu Yuzhi of Shanghai to select 30 young children each year for four years to send to the United States to study various subjects. The first batch selected were Zeng Dugong, Liang Dunyan, Deng Tucong, Cai Jinzhang, Zhang Renkang, Zhong Juncheng, Shi Jintang, Qian Wenkui, He Tingliang, Huang Xibao, Zhan Tianyou, Pan Mingzhong, Cao Jifu, Liu Jiazhao, Zhu Shangzhou, Huang Zhongliang, Mu Yongquan, Cai Shaoji, Huang Kaijia, Shi Jinyong, Chen Ronggui, Cheng Daqi, Ouyang Geng, Chen Jurong, Zhong Wenyao, Wu Yangzeng, Rong Shangqian, Luo Guorui, Tan Yaoxun, and Kuang Rongguang, thirty people in total. They departed in July of the following year. Most of them were from Guangdong Province, accounting for 24 people. The remaining six people were from Jiangsu Province, accounting for three people; Shandong Province, accounting for one person; Anhui Province, accounting for one person; and Fujian Province, accounting for one person. Rong Shangqian and Kuang Rongguang were the youngest, both ten years old. Next were Pan Mingzhong, Zhu Shangzhou, Wu Yangzeng, and Tan Yaoxun, all eleven years old. Then came Zhan Tianyou, Liu Jiazhao, and Luo Guorui, all twelve years old. Then came He Tingliang, Huang Xibao, Cao Jifu, Huang Kaijia, and Chen Jurong, all thirteen years old. The rest were fourteen, fifteen, or sixteen years old. There were none over sixteen years old. Among them, Cao Jifu was from our Chuansha. He went to the United States to study law. After returning to China, he first worked in the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau and later as a clerk in the Shanghai British Magistrate's Office. At that time, the British Magistrate was the Royal Lawyer Wilkinson. Since obtaining Mr. Jifu as a clerk, the host and guests got along well, and he ended his life as a clerk. Mr. Jifu had one son and four daughters. With the income he earned throughout his life, he built five houses and distributed them to his children, which is comparable to Mr. Du Jicheng, a poet of the Ming Dynasty and a fellow villager of our hometown, who built seven houses in one day and gave them to his six sons, keeping one for himself. Mr. Jifu's daughter married Dr. Yan Huiqing of Shanghai. His son went to the United States at a young age to study the navy. After graduating, a certain US Secretary of State, because of his youth and handsomeness, even wanted to marry him to a daughter. He had already been betrothed to a woman in his hometown. At this point, he broke off the engagement and married the American woman. After marrying her, he became a citizen of the United States. He never returned to China. The American government also promoted him and assigned him to the navy. According to the villagers, he has now been promoted to commander of a fleet. So today, there is a Chinese person serving as commander in the US Navy. This is glorious for our country. It is a pity that our country's navy cannot be rejuvenated and made a difference because of a lack of warships and talent and cannot compete with the great powers today. Having gained the heavy trust of the United States and having been promoted to commander of a fleet, he must be a naval talent. Our country has this talent, but it is being used by Jin. This is a great pity for our country. Only sixteen or seventeen years have passed since Mr. Jifu's death, but his wife is still alive. She sometimes receives letters from her son, and she also writes back, but he does not return to China. He will probably live a wealthy and honorable life in the United States and never return to China.

Eating Oranges in Winter and Hygiene 174

— Wan Cheng

In winter, people often reside indoors. The air is stagnant, exercise is lacking, and work is excessive, which can easily lead to constipation and impure blood. Therefore, it is advisable to eat more fruits.

Heaven is truly generous to mankind. In winter, there is the orange, as if intentionally provided for human consumption. Oranges are very rich in plant-based oxygen. The benefits of this oxygen are fivefold: (1) It prevents the retention of uric acid, purifies the blood, and prevents various diseases such as gout, while promoting metabolism. (2) It stimulates the stomach and intestines, facilitating bowel movements and preventing headaches and depression. (3) It moisturizes the throat, preventing coughs and dryness. (4) It cools the heart, spleen, and brain, relieving vexation and irritability. (5) It counteracts the effects of excessive meat consumption, which can lead to poor blood quality. (Westerners always finish their meals with fruit. Formal banquets in our country also include fruit, which reflects the same principle.)

Progress in Reforming Old Operas 175

— Fei

Mei Lanfang's "The Assassin" 176

The play "The Assassin" originates from the Kunqu opera "The Iron Crown," which tells the story of Lady Fei, a palace woman who endures humiliation and lives in hiding, plotting revenge for her lord and country. It conveys a sense of desperation, as it is no easy task for a weak woman to wield a blade and kill a traitor. This play is a classic of Kunqu opera, and many performers are skilled in it. However, during performances, they often fail to fully express its essence. The play's depth requires careful consideration and effort to bring it to life.

Last year, Mei Lanfang's troupe toured America to great success, as everyone knows. "The Assassin" was considered one of their best performances. Mei meticulously researches each play before performing it, never taking the stage lightly. Critics believed that the original script was already excellent, but further attention to facial expressions and movements could elevate it to a world-class drama. Mei agreed and introduced new ideas to the body language and gestures. Although only one scene is truly central to the play, the emotions are fully conveyed and flawless. He performed it in Beijing upon his return, but I could not attend. Now that he has come to Shanghai, I have had the pleasure of hearing his wonderful performance. Remembering the great reputation he earned abroad, I know it was well deserved.

The value of drama lies first in the significance of its subject matter and second in the appropriateness of its structure. "The Assassin" meets both criteria admirably. Chinese operas are often ancient and difficult to verify, making it difficult to evoke empathy from the audience. "The Assassin," set in the late Ming and early Qing dynasties, is relatively recent. The story is based on real events and possesses the spirit of modern drama. Furthermore, China has always been founded on the principles of patriarchal ethics, ritual and teaching virtue. This play, in which a northern woman selflessly risks her life to avenge her country, embodies the spirit of the Eastern nation. The play is a tragedy, naturally performed in a solemn and powerful manner. The structure of the play is concise and focused, preventing the audience from being distracted and allowing them to concentrate. Moreover, Mei Lanfang has carefully revised the play, paying attention to every detail. It is no wonder that the audience is satisfied, and its success is well-deserved. Through this one performance, we can see the excellence of both his voice and his appearance. Moreover, we can explore the progress of reforming old operas. I believe that both modern and traditional drama scholars will study his future performances with even more dedication, not just attending as audience members.

A Record of Visiting the Wedding Hall 177

— Sun Wenwei

On a certain day in the month, my cousin Xu Bangda and Ms. Chen Feiyun were married at the Puyi Agency. The witness was Zhao Shuju, a contemporary epigrapher from Siming. The ceremony, which concluded at three o'clock, was excellent. There were many fine works by Shanghai calligraphers and painters displayed, filling the walls and making it difficult to take them all in. Shen Quanqi's collection of poems by Yuan Zhen and Wu Rong, "Butterflies Seeking Flowers on Trees; Do Not Envy Mandarin Ducks in Paintings," was particularly outstanding. Chu Litang's seal inscription collected from Han dynasty mirror inscriptions, "May your life be as long and good as gold and stone; May your descendants be forever joyful," was also impressive. Liu Weilin's lines, "The morning light from the Wu Mountains connects to the emerald peaks; The clear skies of Jade Peak reflect upon the vermilion railings," were beautiful. Wu Hufan and Feng Chaoran jointly presented a couplet, "May you sing together in harmony for a hundred years; May you be blessed with five generations of prosperity." The characters were written by Hufan in the clerical script, larger than bowls, and very magnificent. Huang Xiaoding's small landscape painting, modeled after a corner of Yan Wengui's long scroll, was inscribed with the four characters "Embroidered Mountains and Rivers." Yao Yuqin's meticulously detailed orchid painting in double outline was inscribed, "The good wind blows and releases the flowers blooming in pairs." Ding Yunxuan's small painting of mandarin ducks and hibiscus was inscribed, "Mandarin Ducks Bring Blessings." Fang Jiekang's calligraphy collected inscriptions from Han dynasty "Eight Sons and Nine Grandsons" mirrors. The text is too long to record. Zhao Xuehou's small painting of hibiscus with old and young children was inscribed, "May you enjoy wealth and honor together in old age." Chen Julai's two red and white seal carvings, the white characters reading "Xu" on the side and the red characters reading "Fu Yin," exhibited an ancient seal script style and a deep understanding of the Qin seal tradition. The marriage certificate was in the style of a single page. The first page featured Zhao Shuju's four large seal characters, "Blessings, Prosperity, Mandarin Ducks." The second page contained Chu Litang's clerical script, "On this auspicious day and time, the marriage ceremony is solemn. May you live together for a hundred years and receive endless blessings." The third page featured Feng Chaoran's daylily painting, inscribed with a poem by an ancient person, "Forget-sorrow grass, daughter flower. Relieving anger is not as good as it. It should be planted in the homes of high officials." The fourth page contained the names of the officiant and witnesses, also written by Mr. Litang. It can be said to be a unique marriage certificate. Bangda paints landscapes following Li Zuishi, figures following Yu Difan, and seal script following Zhao Shuju. He comprehends the essence of their art and progresses rapidly. He is a rare talent among the younger generation. His poems, composed without a teacher, are also fresh and readable, revealing his intelligence.

Travelogue of Southeast Asia (98) 178

— Linghua

Again, I saw several people gathered around watching. One person was using a needle to pierce people's skin, applying colored paint to the needle and pricking it into the skin to create various designs. This is what is called tattooing. The designs are often in the shape of animals, birds, insects, or reptiles like snakes and centipedes. This is rare in northern China, but it exists in the area south of the Huai River. It is prevalent in Fujian and Guangdong and very common overseas. People who do not wear clothes often consider skin patterns to be beautiful, which has led to a kind of superstition and become a form of social expression. Generally, in China, it is more common among laborers and in the Jiangsu and Zhejiang societies. I don't know about here.

The custom of women piercing their noses and ears is prevalent here, but it seems to be more common among Indian and Burmese people. The ear piercings sometimes create large holes, severely damaging the ears, which is a barbaric custom. Some modern men and women here also cut their hair, while the older generation does not, just like in China.

The houses in Rangoon are not as good as those in Penang and are more old-fashioned. Singapore is magnificent, and Penang is elegant but smaller. Rangoon is even less impressive. This is because Singapore and Penang are newly developed colonies, while Rangoon is an ancient capital. Singapore has 400,000 Chinese residents, while Penang has only one-third of that number. Rangoon has only about ten thousand Chinese residents. The scale of its chambers of commerce and schools is much smaller than those in Singapore and Penang. At night, the Shwedagon Pagoda and the White Pagoda in Rangoon are lit up with electric lights, which are very similar to the Sincere and Wing On Companies in Shanghai. However, the influence of the Buddhist pagodas is significant.

There are many mosquitoes in northern Burma that can cause illness by biting people. In some places, people have died from snake bites. I heard that many people are still injured by snakes in India every year.

European Travel Correspondence (89) 179

— Liu Haisu

Diary of a Pilgrimage to Italy

(III) Ten Days in Rome (X) (2)

June 4th - The Grand Cathedral of Saint Peter - The Vatican Palace - The Sistine Chapel -

The Vatican Palace is a world-renowned treasury. It lies to the west of Rome, on the right bank of the Tiber River. The towering Saint Peter's Basilica stands in front. There are numerous strange and magnificent buildings, sculptures, and paintings that move the world. The most famous are the architecture of Saint Peter's Basilica and the frescoes of the Sistine Chapel. Saint Peter was the most famous of Christ's twelve apostles. He accepted Christ's mission and preached Christianity in Rome, ultimately sacrificing himself for God. His remains are buried in Rome. Legend has it that a church was built above Saint Peter's tomb in the second century. In the fourth century, after Emperor Constantine legalized Christianity as the state religion, a more magnificent church was rebuilt over Peter's tomb. The marble used to decorate the interior of the church was transported from Hadrian's Mausoleum.

In 1500, Pope Julius II expanded the sanctuary of Saint Peter's Basilica, commissioning the great architect Bramante to begin the project. Unfortunately, this great work was left unfinished when Bramante died. Later, under Pope Leo X, the project was repaired by the great masters Raphael and Michelangelo. It was finally completed by Bernini after hundreds of years, with designs by numerous masters, resulting in the most magnificent spectacle in architectural history. Now, let me recall our visit to this world's greatest sanctuary.

When the Roman sun was shining brightly on the dry streets, we packed our bags and left the hotel. We took the tram from the sunlit, stone-paved square straight to the Vatican. After about ten minutes, we reached the end of the tram line. As soon as we got off, the view suddenly opened up. A white stone plain stood before us. In the center stood a towering, pointed obelisk, so high it seemed to touch the clouds. On either side stood two large fountains, spewing water dozens of feet into the air like a flood, reflecting the sunlight. We walked happily to the square, surrounded by countless huge stone columns arranged in four rows like a cloister. Suddenly, in the center, a huge dome, four hundred feet high, rose majestically into the sky, shining brilliantly. This was the dome of Saint Peter's Basilica. At that moment, I thought to myself that the person who could conceive of such a strange and magnificent idea must have been the great Michelangelo. Later research confirmed that this was indeed Michelangelo's masterpiece. Filled with a sense of satisfaction and longing, we slowly walked up dozens of stone steps to the main entrance of Saint Peter's Basilica. The front corridor of the entrance has twenty-four columns, arranged in two rows. Each column is one hundred and sixty-five feet high, and its circumference is large enough for fifteen people to encircle. The columns are all made of granite. As we stood between these enormous columns and looked back at the colonnades on both sides, everyone would exclaim in amazement.

Such large columns stand side by side, supporting the stone beams. Above the eaves stand huge stone statues of Christ and his twelve disciples, so imposing and majestic that they seem to boast of the grand spectacle of ancient architecture.

Financial Gold Market Unleashes Its Fury 180

Leaping by a Huge Seventeen Taels

The Surge... Overwhelming Like a Tidal Wave

The Shorts... Lamenting Their Impending Doom

A Record Peak of Forty-Nine Taels Emerges, Yesterday, December 12th, New Gold Market Records Appear Endlessly, Almost Reaching 650 Taels. An Unprecedented Peak. The Intensity of the Bull Run Shows No Sign of Stopping. The Whole City is Shaken. Extreme Panic. Furious Waves. Fluctuations of Four or Five Taels at Every Turn. The Public is Appalled. Almost No Time to React. Throughout the Day, a Total Reversal of Sixteen or Seventeen Taels. The Morning Market Oscillated Between Twelve and Thirteen Taels. Demand Exceeded Supply in Trading Amongst Peers. Short Sellers Were Eager to Cover, But There Was No Way Out. Sin Heng, Wing Hing, Yuan Mao Yong, and Others Were Buying. Dalian Gang, Xie Yu, Yuan Heng, and Others Were Selling Their Positions. Even Though the Overseas Silver Market Rose Slightly, It Was Not Affected. Gold Prices Reached a High Point. Suddenly, Exchange Rates Soared and Fluctuated Wildly, Jumping More Than Ten Taels, Exceeding the Forty Taels Mark. However, Due to Differing Transactions, There Were Four Taels of Oscillation. The Afternoon Market Was Even More Perilous, With Price Differences of Five or Six Taels. Sin Heng and Wing Hing Continued to Compete for Purchases. Exchange Rates Were Particularly Strong. The Market Condition Became Increasingly Tight. Afterward, It Approached the Fifty Taels Mark. The Momentum Was Terrifying, Unstoppable. It Seemed Like There Was No End in Sight. This Morning's Large Bars Were Still Expecting Lower Prices.

Astonishing Changes Occurred One After Another. This Morning, the Opening Price for January Was 633 Taels, A Jump of Two Taels (Gross Prices Were 30 to 33.4, But Trading Was Chaotic, Mostly More Buying Than Selling). The Large Silver Bars and Silver Prices Only Increased by an Eighth. Exchange Rates Dropped by a Sixteenth. Private Telegrams Also Fell by a Sixteenth. Silver Prices Remained Unchanged. Public Confidence Remained Strong. It Did Not Have an Impact. There Were Fluctuations of One or Two Taels. It Once Reached 32.5. The Momentum Behind Buying Was Strong. Yarn and Cotton Yarn Market Plunges Sharply 185

The yarn market is very weak, with a sharp decline. The overseas cotton yarn market is uniformly trending downwards. The local market was already pessimistic, and under the impact of this trend, it will be even more difficult to sustain. People are increasingly fearful, and there is a sense of rapid decline. The future remains uncertain.

Numerous Bidding Sellers Emerge. The opening of the bidding market was driven by a sharp drop in American cotton, leading to significant market unease. Sellers flocked to the market, and Jardine Matheson sold unlimited quantities, causing an even steeper decline. The current month fell by 1.29 taels, and the distant months fell by 0.09 taels. It was reported in the afternoon that spot sales were sluggish, and third-grade yarn fell sharply by 3-4 yuan. As a result, market sentiment remained weak, and various months fell by 0.01-0.09 taels. The total daily trading volume was 29,950 bales. Grain and Flour Market Temporarily Trends Sideways 188

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market in the morning and afternoon, the various months generally trended sideways. The initial openings for each month were relatively good, but as the quoted prices for foreign wheat fell only slightly, the sentiment outside the industry was inevitably somewhat soft. However, due to the lack of factory sales, the overall trend only felt stagnant. Until the afternoon opening, due to rumors of a rebound in gold coins, the market sentiment for near and far term contracts rebounded slightly. According to speculation within the industry, the current situation can be sustained. If actual sales are smooth or if it triggers purchasing interest from the Northern and Southern groups, this month may improve, which is also unknown. As a result, the current month was down by 0.0025 taels compared to the previous day, January to March were up by 0.0025 taels each, and April and May were unchanged.

Wheat Futures Rise Only Slightly 189

Yesterday, after the opening of the wheat futures market in the morning and afternoon, the various months again showed a firm trend. Although the quoted prices for foreign wheat fell slightly by 0.002-0.004 taels, the sharp contraction of foreign exchange has made the prospect of ordering foreign wheat currently scarce, leading to a firm rise in some people's sentiment. Those who were short-selling were also seen to be timid. In the afternoon, the market sentiment was even tighter due to another sharp rise in the gold market. However, large short-selling firms were still calm on the surface because they still had prepared foreign wheat on order, resulting in only a slight increase. As a result, the current month was up by 0.03 taels compared to the previous day, January was up by 0.01 taels, February was up by 0.02 taels, and March, April, and May were each up by 0.03 taels. The spot wheat market was silent, with only 300 bags of Xianghe wheat opening, with prices down 0.01 taels compared to before.

Sugar Market Soars Again 191

Foreign Exchange Higher, Tax Increase Imminent

Private Telegram: Java Sugar Expected to Rise by One Guilder

Japanese Sugar Mills Take Advantage, Offer Significant Quantities

Yesterday's sugar market reports from producing areas: Cuban spot sugar price remained at 1.375, New York sugar futures were at 1.30 for December, 1.43 for March of next year, 1.50 for May, and 1.64 for September. Compared to the previous report, only May fell slightly by 0.01, and other months did not fluctuate. Java spot and futures sugar prices did not rise or fall. The guild drew plates in view of the higher foreign exchange rate, reports of an increase in tariffs to be implemented on January 1, and a private telegram stating that prices in Java were expected to rise by one guilder. Tate & Lyle Sugar also cabled that they would not sell. Market sentiment was tense as a result, and buying interest became more intense. Market prices suddenly soared: Dutch sugar No. 24 coarse white rose 8.4 taels, No. 20 medium white 7.6 taels, No. 18 rose 7.5 taels, No. 8 Dutch red rose 6.925 to 7 taels, and No. 10 rose 7.1 taels, with the market at 7.2 taels in the late afternoon. The market was brisk. Japanese sugar prices also tended sharply upward: N Mark price reached 8.85 taels, YT Mark 8.5 to 8.55 taels, TK Mark 8.7 taels, YRO Mark price from 8.05 to 8.1 taels, and YP Mark price from 9 to 9.05 taels, with the market as high as 9.1 taels in the late afternoon. Transactions were active, and the market was quite firm. Japanese sugar mills took advantage of the situation and offered significant quantities: Meiji Sugar offered 40,000 bags at 4.5 Japanese yen, with higher and lower grades adjusted proportionally. Minghua Sugar offered 10,000 bags at 6 yuan, including tax, all for February delivery. Yanshui Port New Factory also offered December and January delivery, ET and ER marks paired at 4,000 bags, priced at 4.9 Japanese yen. Dazheng Factory offered January and February delivery, AW and AR marks in equal quantities, totaling 5,000 bags priced at 4.75 Japanese yen. The new tax increase made them quite popular. The Haopan factory also opened the Nanyang Factory's ice product factory at the original plate price and market was extremly brisks, and there were already talks of a price increase. In the spot market, Fuka Foreign Firm sold 1,000 bags of medium white sugar at 7.4 taels. The goods were slightly inferior, so the price was more affordable.

Yesterday, the white tung oil market showed strength again. As the end of the year approaches, Chinese merchants will undertake futures sales for export, and market sentiment is slightly firm. However, it is still difficult to improve selling prices. Domestic sales have become exhausted. The end-grade category has had many sources arriving from Hankou, and actual sales are smooth. Hardware English White Iron Sales Smooth 193

English white iron, regardless of color, has recently been trending very smoothly. Prices are rising steadily due to supply shortages. Currently, 22-gauge sells for up to 13.55 taels per dan, 24-gauge for 14 taels, 26-gauge for 15.75 taels, 28-gauge for 15.95 taels, and 48 sheets for 16.75 taels, 0.5-0.6 taels higher than the previous market. Export groups, such as those from inland and along the Yangtze River, are still seeking to deliver goods, but the northern groups have little trading due to the approaching New Year. The local construction group has the strongest appetite, with an estimated 300-400 bundles being opened in the past two or three days. The circulation of goods is increasingly scarce, so market sentiment is solid. The future standard has a good chance of continuing to improve.

Silk and Tea Double Palace Silk Sales Brisk, Prices Rise 194

This year, silkworm production in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces has been poor, and fresh cocoon prices are high. Villagers in various areas sell cocoons instead of reeling silk, resulting in a shortage of raw silk materials needed by silk weaving factories. In addition, raw silk prices are gradually rising, and silk merchants are purchasing double palace silk. Recently, spring silk weaving has begun, and the demand for raw materials is high. Sales of double palace silk are brisk. The six double palace silk factories in the Shanghai area are almost unable to meet demand. Silk prices are gradually rising, with high-quality double palace silk initially rising from 420 taels to 480 taels, and now rising another 10 taels. The market is quite brisk.

Foreign Tea Market In a Tailspin 195

Yesterday, the foreign tea market in this city remained quiet. The sales of Zhenmei green tea from both Lu Zhuang and Tu Zhuang were increasingly sluggish. Although the American Zhuang have a few stomach intake of Xia Mu Zhu tea, market trading remained low. Transactions of Zhen Mei and Xiu Mei teas have also become more sluggish. British and French merchants are generally tightening their belts due to the impending year end and weak overseas sales. The tea market trend seems in a tailspin.

Art World

After Viewing the Shanghai Art College Painting Exhibition 197

— Lou Jinsheng

In these past three months, there have been two or three painting exhibitions in a row, which is very gratifying. Recently, the Shanghai Art College on Jiangwan Road in Zhabei held another painting exhibition, which opened on the 11th of this month. On display were student works, faculty works, and works by Japanese artists, totaling eight hundred and several tens of pieces. President Wang Daoyuan is said to have studied at the Tokyo Art School in Japan for many years. The professors, such as Chen Baoyi, Zhu Yingpeng, and Ni Yide, are all well-known artists. The addition of works by Japanese artists to the exhibition makes it very worthwhile to see.

I rushed there at nine o'clock on the morning of the 11th. At that time, everything was not yet fully arranged, but the paintings were all hung up, so I was not disappointed. Among the works, Chen Baoyi's landscapes still have the same style and taste. He still likes to use green and rough brushstrokes. One small landscape is very well painted. The light and colors of the water and mountains in the painting are extraordinarily shocking and complex, but he handles them very well, still using a relaxed and light brushstroke. I feel that the author is worthy of admiration. Secondly, Ni Yide's paintings have undergone a major change in style. He uses large brushstrokes and simple colors. "Eating Utensils" is the best piece. Recently, I often talk to friends about how the most difficult time for a painter is after more than ten years of white study. When a person reaches this time, there is little progress. Looking at our current art scene, there are the most of these people, which is very sad, because he has been bound by what he has learned himself. Therefore, I think it is a good idea for Ni Yide to change his style.

Regarding Wang Daoyuan's works, his method of expression is very unique. One portrait of a Japanese woman has extremely beautiful brushwork. A portrait of a Chinese woman has an outstanding way of painting the woman's face. However, I feel that the painting sometimes lacks cleanliness, but the painting "On the Road to Lingyin" rarely has this problem. Zhu Yingpeng's "Earth Mother" has a different kind of interest. The face of the Earth Mother is painted very movingly.

Regarding the Japanese painters, there is a "Nude Woman" and "Suzhou River Wharf," the author's name has been forgotten. "Nude Woman" shows the ambiguity in the painting studio, and "Suzhou River Wharf" uses a gloomy tone and a very novel method of expression.

After seeing the exhibition, I thought about all kinds of things. I feel that there are too few writings on painting now, it is really too lonely. Therefore, despite my own shallowness, I wrote this article.

Japanese Imperial Art Exhibition of Western Paintings Tour (2) 198

— Xie Haiyan

Japan Correspondence

The stone steps and the plaza in front of the Tokyo Prefectural Art Museum were already crowded with people. Besides a large number of male visitors, there were also two or three groups of female students and elementary school children. Someone who hadn't seen this before would surely find it amusing, thinking, "What do children know? Yet they happily come to art exhibitions like this." Actually, in Japan, where art education is widespread, this is not an unusual sight. Whether walking on the street, in a park, by the seaside, or in the countryside, one can always find two or three children standing, squatting, or sitting, one hand holding a brush, the other holding a drawing board, applying reds and greens as they sketch from nature. Some of them paint quite well, displaying a pure and innocent expression, and they also understand a little about art principles, the relationship between light and color, and the principles of perspective. One day, I went for a stroll in Hibiya Park and happened to look up to see a large crowd forming a semi-circular human screen, intently appreciating a student who appeared to be from an art school, depicting the towering Public Hall.

"......The painting is not bad, but the color and tone... what do you think?"

"That's right, he probably didn't pay attention to the atmosphere..." Two not-so-small elementary school students emerged from the crowd and made this incisive criticism on their way home, which left me stunned. Anything can happen; even children know what is called 'tone' and what is called 'atmosphere'! This happened in February of this year, and the impression it left on me is still vivid in my memory.

In Ueno, the art capital of Japan, exhibitions by various art groups, large and small, are regularly held, month after month, without fail. From the opening day to the closing day, there is not a single exhibition that is not filled with small visitors of this kind. They diligently hold a small booklet of exhibit titles and a small pencil, starting from the first room in the exhibition hall, appreciating each painting with an open mind and in silence. When they find a painting they like and find beautiful, they mark it with a circle on the catalog. If they like it even more, they draw several circles in a row. Conversely, for paintings they deem bad or unattractive, paintings they dislike, they mark an "X" next to the item’s name and the artist’s name to express their dissatisfaction. Older children not only draw circles or "X" marks but also jot down a few comments next to the entry in the catalog, expressing their opinions on the painting. Their method of appreciation is also very skillful. They know to move forward to study the brushstrokes and color harmony in detail, and they also know to step back to view the overall structure and the totality of colors in the entire painting. Sometimes moving forward, sometimes stepping back, sometimes closing one eye, sometimes making a telescope shape with their hands, they do their utmost in the art of appreciation. From this, we can see a glimpse of the aesthetic sense of the Japanese people.

However, I do not like to view paintings in a room with children, especially groups of children. If they are with companions, they are extremely noisy and prone to bumping and barging about. Fortunately, although I coincidentally encountered these groups of elementary school students pouring into the entrance at the same time today, they all turned left, heading first to the first section, the Japanese painting exhibition hall. We, on the other hand, began with the second section on the right, the Western painting exhibition.

Upon entering the room, one cannot help but feel a gloomy and dense atmosphere, as if entering a dark cave where it is impossible to find a source of light. To put it plainly, the current Imperial Exhibition has reached the extreme of vulgarity and corruption. The artists of the Imperial Exhibition, because they want to enjoy the benefits of being given all favorable treatment by the government-sponsored exhibition, devote all their efforts to surface embellishment, using it to attract the worship of ordinary people – outsiders – and further consolidate the foundation of the fortress they have built up over the years. This absurd mistake has resulted in these two self-digging, tomb-creating disasters:

1. The hardening of thought, and

2. The vulgarization of technique.

The Imperial Exhibition – even its predecessor, the Ministry of Education Fine Arts Exhibition (文展), which is the fine arts exhibition of the Ministry of Education – was founded in the late Meiji era, in the fortieth year [of Meiji, 1907]. In the eighth year of the Taisho era [1919], under the tide of ardent reform arguments, the Imperial Academy of Fine Arts was established, and the Ministry of Education exhibition (文展) was renamed the Imperial Exhibition (帝展). Since its inception, it has had a long history of over twenty years. However, the anti-traditional school of thought at the time of its founding was discriminatory toward artistic styles after Impressionism. Works that were not in the style of academic realism could rarely, almost absolutely never, be selected. Later, new and upcoming artists did not approve of the examiners' judgment, and as a result, the revolutionary Nikakai was established. They rallied like-minded individuals, raised the flag of "anti-government exhibition," and broke away from the stagnant, dogmatic, and non-individualistic fetters of the Western painting world of the past, embarking on a path of true, interesting, free, and individually enlightened art.

Midway through – in the early days of the Imperial Exhibition – although gradually succumbing to the times, it changed its examination policy. Works that could not pass selection during the Ministry of Education exhibition were also selectively adopted, giving the Nikakai a victory of foresight. However, the position of not adopting the most radical schools of painting, such as Cubism, Futurism, Constructivism, Expressionism, and Surrealism, is still adhered to to this day. Originally, since government endeavors cannot be more radical than general endeavors, there is probably an unavoidable reason for this. But if it is too far from the times, I believe it is not appropriate. (To be continued)

Youth Corner

Great China University Student Social Gathering 200

— Xiang

Held Tonight at 7 PM

Time flies like an arrow. This semester has passed by quickly and busily. Generally, the passionate and youthful students, immersed in the mechanical school life, naturally feel mentally bored. Therefore, the pursuit of love and the moans of literature and art are their expressions. However, this is not universal and cannot be enjoyed by everyone. Therefore, students from various schools, in order to remedy the shortcomings of this peculiar paradise and to seek common warmth and connect with the feelings of the masses, are holding social gatherings. Especially as the end of the semester approaches, who doesn't feel the dryness of the taste of books over the past few months? Therefore, the variety shows of various schools have been held one after another. It is known that the social gathering of students from Great China University is scheduled to be held in the auditorium of the university at 7 PM on the 13th of this month. The Chinese Harmonica Team, the Shanghai National Martial Arts Hall, and the Plum Blossom Girls' Dance Troupe have been invited to perform. It is heard that Xu Zexiang and others in charge of the gathering are quite busy with preparations. It is expected that there will be a grand scene at that time.

A Night's Talk on the Question of After Graduation 201

— Yun

The evening was dim, and the north wind was blowing fiercely in the sky. The figures in the dining hall were sparse. Only a few dozen of us occupied about ten tables eating dinner. This was because today was Saturday. Those who had families in Shanghai or places to go had already gone out. So only a few dozen of us were scattered about having dinner.

After the meal, I felt even more bored. The four people in my room had gone out and hadn't returned yet. They had families in Shanghai, so they probably wouldn't be back tonight. There were two others left, but they were classmates from junior high school, and I couldn't really talk to them about anything. It was really stifling. Boredom filled my heart with all sorts of thoughts, making me extremely sad. I wanted to suppress these mixed thoughts, but the more I tried to suppress them, the more mixed thoughts arose. I had no way to deal with it, so I quietly strolled to a classroom where there wasn't a single soul. But not a moment later, Miss Zhou, Miss Li, and Miss Lin from my class suddenly came in. They pushed the door open with laughter. I couldn't help but be startled by them.

"Miss Wang, you're so leisurely, hiding here all alone. What are you thinking about? Are you thinking about him?" Miss Li saw me and asked with a mischievous grin. Then Miss Zhou said,

"You made us search so hard! We went to your fancy room and found it empty. So you're here, thinking about what?"

"Thinking about what? Are you making fun of me too? What is there on my mind that I can't tell you? Isn't it what we talked about yesterday?"

"What did you talk about yesterday? I didn't! You were talking about something without letting me know!" Miss Lin said, pouting like a child.

"Miss Lin is always like a child, having another childish outburst. Where did you run off to? We looked for you there," Miss Li said, arguing with her.

"Forget it, let me tell you. Yesterday evening, when Miss Li and I were walking in the campus, we suddenly ran into Miss Zhou and Miss Bu, who were also walking in the campus. The four of us formed a group, and we sat in the campus and discussed. It was mainly about our future. Talking about the future is really a headache, making us unable to start. We talked for an hour or two yesterday, but we didn't come to any conclusions. We started talking about the nearest future, but that is a terrible future. We are all about to graduate from senior high school teacher training, so the problem of our nearest future is naturally the problem of after graduation. What a difficult problem this is!"

"Yes, my family, to put it bluntly, is certainly a well-to-do family, but because there are too many people in the family, my hope of going to college will probably become a despair. It's not that I don't want to pursue higher education, but the environment is forcing me. I am going to fall behind, and I'm sorry if I will disappoint you. Perhaps my heart still doesn't want to fall behind. Although I don't have the qualification to enjoy formal college education, no one can stop me from studying advanced knowledge in practice," Miss Lin said to this point, her eyes already turning red, seeming about to shed tears. Then Miss Zhou also excitedly said,

"Miss Lin, we are both in the same boat. I also can't go to college. The reason is none other than being controlled by the environment. That's why I often can't go on when I talk to you about these things. It's not that I want to keep my family circumstances a secret, but I really don't have the courage to say it. Now that you've all talked about these things, let me also speak my mind. In terms of my environment, first, my family is not very wealthy, and second, my parents don't believe in girls studying, so from the time I graduated from elementary school until now, I have relied on my own strong will and worked hard to win my parents' consent. However, in these few years, my parents have repeatedly said to me, 'Qin'er,

Page 26

your neighbors are getting old and are eager for you to get married, and hope that you can understand the hearts of the two elders, and don't be so determined to keep going to school.' My reply is, 'Dad, Mom, please don't say these words. I know my own life, and I will always obey you, so please rest assured.' So after graduating from senior high school teacher training this time, I can't continue to go against their wishes. I know that even if I continue to argue, I'm afraid I won't be successful. It's better to temporarily end my studies. At the same time, to take care of economic problems, I want to work for a year before deciding. But whether I can find a way to continue my studies after that is naturally a problem."

As they talked to this point, the hot tears that filled each of their eyes fell like beads from a broken string at the same time. All that could be heard was sobbing. There was some silence in between, and it's hard to describe what the scene was like. They left the classroom together in sadness.

Alas, I wonder how many young people are out of school. Judging from the proportion of us few people, it's really alarming! Just a few minutes ago, how could I have known that none of us few had hope of going to college? Is this fate controlling us, or is it the inherited social system that is bullying us? And what attitude should we take?

I wonder how many young men and women are troubled by disappointment, sad because of trouble, and moving towards the path of negativity because of sadness. This has created the arrogance of youth. But should we be like this? No, the youth of the times should never be like this! We should resist the destructive force of the environment's potential. We should work even harder in disappointment to achieve our future goals. I think a bright future is definitely waiting for us. If we are willing to work hard with determination and double our efforts, temporary disappointment can never prevent our great success in the future.

The 18th Issue of Era Youth 202

The Era Youth, edited by the Era Youth Society, has been very successful since its publication and has been praised by the general youth. Moreover, the publication date is extremely reliable, breaking the bad habits of the current publishing industry. The 18th issue has now been published on schedule. The contents include "The Characteristics of Soviet Russian Civil Law," "Era Youth and the National Movement," "Before Departure," "The Flower Seller," "Melancholy" (continued), "News from the Society," etc., all of which are must-reads for young people. It is sold by Shanghai Ximen Daguang Bookstore, the general agent, and major bookstores in this city and other places, as well as school numbers in Shanghai, are all agents for sale. It is also heard that the subscription is 45 cents for half a year and 80 cents for the whole year, postage included.

Writing to Bao Jun (continued) 203

— Cheng Bishui

Alas, Bao Jun, is this really seeking one's own death? I am unwilling to say this, I am unwilling to say this! If I work hard at selling manuscripts, it's not impossible to make a living. But, Bao Jun, the current me has neither fame, nor money, nor a woman. Who would be willing to rely on selling articles to make a living?

Alas, Bao Jun, just talking about it makes me want to shed tears again. I have already told you before that I only have one bamboo cloth long gown to wear. Besides this, I have no second set of clothes to change into. But that Miss, she (I don't know her surname and name, but her family lives at 161 XX Road. Let's use 161 to represent her for now), I meet her in the French Park every day, and she changes into a different outfit every day.

Alas, alas, Bao Jun, there is probably no sadness in the world greater than this. I am really seeking my own troubles. Both of us are in tune with each other, but why can't I directly go to her and express my love? I would feel satisfied only when I’m sitting in her arms. It doesn’t matter even if I kneel at her feet, but why can’t I do this?

Oh, I understand, Bao Jun. It's not that I don't have the courage to do it, but social forces don't allow me to do it, and economic conditions don't allow me to do it. It's pitiful to be in this old society, and I'm also a poor scholar. Like this, I am not qualified to love the person I want to love.

Alas, alas, Bao Jun, I remember, you once said to me that you thought the prerequisite for love was that the problem of life should be solved first, otherwise it would just be empty talk. If one is hungry oneself, then one cannot blame anyone. If one marries a woman, and she also goes hungry with oneself, then the woman has not committed any sin. One cannot harm her. Continued on the ninth page

Page 27

Then, the woman has no fault at all, and I cannot harm her.

Alas, alas, thinking of these words makes me feel sad again. Pitiful me, lately I can't even eat a meal. Sometimes there isn't even a drop of water to drink in a day. Like this, I cannot solve my own life problems. I don’t have the ability to maintain myself. And she, she, Bao Jun, I have already told you before, her family has three or four servants. Their servants don't even go hungry. It's pitiful that my life is not as comfortable as the servants in her family. How can I dare to love her?

Alas, alas, I am ashamed to death, Bao Jun. I was wrongly born a man. But when I think of my current situation, my tears are less valuable than a woman's, dripping down and wetting my blue shirt.

Alas, Bao Jun, I don't know if it was intentional or unintentional, but she, who lives at 161 XX Road, one day in the French Park, seeing me following her, deliberately dropped her silk handkerchief on the grass. Later, I ran over to pick it up, and saw the three letters S.C.M. embroidered on it. I don't know if she deliberately left it for me. But me, Bao Jun, pitifully, my handkerchief is just a silk gauze product, bought from the Sanyou Industrial Company, one dime a piece. I want to return the favor, but I'm embarrassed to take it out.

Hand Water Outfit 204

— Taken by Bing

Several times I wanted to launch a fierce attack on her, to start a conversation with her first. But I am a coward, I am a content person. Before I even opened my mouth to speak to her, my heart would jump nervously, and redness would instantly appear on my cheeks. At this time, I was so ashamed that there was no place for me to hide. How could I have the courage to open my mouth to speak to her like this?

Once, there was a very good opportunity. She and I ran into each other on the road. She even glanced at me several times, looking me up and down, seeming like she wanted to talk to me (I don't dare say that she was prepared to talk to me, so I use the words "seeming like"). A person with courage would have already stepped forward to greet her. But me, Bao Jun, I am a coward after all. Pitifully, at this time, I could only scurry away like a rabbit. I didn't dare to boldly step forward and greet her shamelessly. This was really missing a good opportunity. I really missed a good opportunity.

Since that time, when I go to the French Park, I no longer see her beautiful figure. Alas, has she abandoned me? Or is she complaining that I am too cowardly? Or else, is she sick? ...... Pitiful me, I can't directly run to 161 XX Road and ask her in person why she doesn't come to the French Park. I have no way of knowing. At this time, I am really in extreme pain.

Alas, according to reason, getting sick doesn't seem to be so coincidental. Abandoning me, I haven't even spoken to her, let alone offended her. Of course, she wouldn't abandon me for no reason. I understand, Bao Jun, she must be complaining that I am too cowardly. She must be complaining that I am too cowardly...

But although she doesn't go to the French Park anymore, I still have a chance to meet her every day when I walk past the door of 161 XX Road, as long as she is at home. But, Bao Jun, this is another very awkward thing. When I walk past the door of her house, if she sees me, she always tries to avoid me. But after I pass the door of her house, she stands at the door again to look at me. If I turn back to look at her and our eyes meet, then she, like me, has both cheeks flushed red. From this point of observation, I am able to be sure that she has my impression in her mind. (To be continued)
